<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper introduces a two-dimensional localization system for passive UHF RFID transponders based on phase-of-arrival evaluation of the backscattered tag signal. A multiple-channel system, where alternately one path is configured as a transmitter and the remaining paths work as receivers, is used to permit the position estimation. To improve localization accuracy and reduce disturbances caused by multipath propagation, a frequency-stepped continuous-waveform approach is employed. To achieve proof of concept, a local position measurement system demonstrator comprising an RFID reader, passive EPC Gen 2 RFID tags, several transceivers, baseband hardware, and signal processing was used for measurements. The results show excellent localization accuracy, even in an indoor environment.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Localization, tracking, and identification of objects are important tasks in numerous modern applications. Although each individual information can be obtained by various measurement techniques, only a few methods fulfill the requirements of simultaneous localization and data transmission while maintaining low cost and power consumption.</p><p>Local position measurement systems often rely on radio-wave data transfer between numerous base stations and active transponders attached to the target objects <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. These systems achieve high accuracy, but they suffer from limited battery lifetime and high costs of the active tags.</p><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) is widely used in electronic identification and tracking; recent techniques in RFID localization generally derive estimates of tag positions from the signal strength received by stationary readers <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. Especially for passive tags, this technique is usually imprecise because signal strength depends on environmental conditions, tag orientation, and multipath propagation. Other RFID localization systems rely on phase evaluation of the backscattered transponder signal, but they are either not capable of localizing passive RFID tags with only one stationary reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a> or only with the constraint of moving transponders <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a>.</p><p>In this paper, a two-dimensional (2-D) position measurement system for passive UHF RFID tags using phase-of-arrival (PoA) evaluation of the backscattered tag signal is presented. To improve localization accuracy and reduce disturbances caused by multipath propagation, a frequency-stepped continuous-waveform (FSCW) approach is employed that can be realized without modification of the off-the-shelf RFID reader. In contrast to the system described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a>, where one transmit antenna and several receive antennas were used to achieve position measurement in an anechoic chamber, multiple transceiver channels are used in the current system. More precisely, alternately, one path is configured as a transmitter, and the remaining paths work as receivers. Therefore, a higher number of signal paths can be achieved for a reduced number of antennas. Based on existing EPC Gen 2 UHF RFID tags, a local position measurement system demonstrator comprising one off-the-shelf RFID reader, several transceiver channels, baseband hardware, and signal processing was used to prove the system concept based on measurements carried out in an indoor environment. Compared with the currently popular technique of localization using the received signal strength, this system shows better accuracy and sensitivity.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>System Description</h2></div><p>The basic concept of the position measurement system for passive UHF RFID transponders relies on PoA evaluation of the backscattered tag signal. During the response period of the tag, an RFID reader transmits a continuous wave (CW) signal in a defined frequency range at alternately one of the channels of the system demonstrator. An RFID transponder communicates with the reader by means of backscatter modulation, where the tag switches the reflection coefficient of its antenna between two states in accordance with the data being sent. This backscattered tag signal is received by the antennas located in the remaining channels, amplified by low-noise amplifiers (LNA), down-converted to baseband, and recorded by analog-to-digital converters (ADCs). The PoA of the backscattered tag signal is estimated at each receiver and represents the ambiguous length of the propagation path from the transmit antenna to the receive antenna via the RFID tag, thus allowing a localization of the tag. As there is a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2\pi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Ï<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">2\pi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> ambiguity in phase measurements, a multiple number of path lengths exist that result in the estimated PoA. To increase localization accuracy, the frequency of the CW signal is changed for each measurement; more precisely, a linear but stepped frequency ramp is performed. By means of this FSCW principle, the length of the propagation path can be calculated unambiguously <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_2">[14]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_2">[15]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a>. However, since the bandwidth of UHF RFID is tightly limited in most regions, only a suppression in multipath disturbances can be achieved.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurement Apparatus</h2></div><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Schematic representation of the position measurement system consisting of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-5" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> channels.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The position measurement system consists of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> channels, where alternately one path is configured as transmitter and the remaining paths work as receivers. The transmit signal is generated by an off-the-shelf RFID reader using a standardized protocol for the identification of passive UHF RFID tags. A directional coupler in the transmission line feeds a power divider that splits the signal to provide the local oscillator (LO) inputs of quadrature demodulators, one located in each channel. The transmit signal then supports the common port of an <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-way antenna switch, which is, in collaboration with two-way switches, in charge of the selection of the transmit path. The RF inputs of the quadrature demodulators are provided by signals received by the antennas of the remaining channels, which are amplified by low-noise amplifiers (LNAs). The resulting IQ intermediate-frequency (IF) output signals of the demodulator are acquired simultaneously by a multichannel ADC card. A schematic diagram of the system architecture is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Signal Model</h2></div><p>As previously mentioned, the basic concept of the position measurement system for passive UHF RFID tags relies on PoA evaluation of the backscattered transponder signal, which represents the ambiguous length of the signal path. Unfortunately, in addition to the influence of the tag position to the PoA, there also is a dependency on the tag orientation.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Influence of Tag Position</h3><p>The transmit signal of the RFID reader is alternately switched to one of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-14" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula> channels of the system demonstrator. The signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm Tx},k}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-17" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; At each of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M-1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">M-1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> remaining channels, which are configured as receivers, both a time-delayed <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\tau_{2,l}, \tau_{3,k,l})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">(\tau_{2,l}, \tau_{3,k,l})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and damped <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\alpha_{2,l}, \alpha_{3,k,l})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">(\alpha_{2,l}, \alpha_{3,k,l})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> copy of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm BS},k}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">s_{{\rm BS},k}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm Tx},k}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">s_{{\rm Tx},k}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is received. The resulting signal is amplified by an LNA and can be modeled by <disp-formula id="deqn4-6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{s_{{\rm RF},k,l}(t) = &amp;\, \alpha_{2,l} s_{{\rm BS},k}(t-\tau_{2,l}) \cr &amp; \quad + \alpha_{3,k,l} s_{{\rm Tx},k}(t-\tau_{3,k,l}) &amp;{\hbox{(4)}}\cr\tau_{2,l} = &amp;\, {{\Vert {\bf z}_{\rm Tag}- {\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l} \Vert_{2}}\over {c_{0}}} &amp;{\hbox{(5)}}\cr\tau_{3,k,l} = &amp;\, {{\Vert {\bf z}_{{\rm Tx},k}- {\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l} \Vert_{2}}\over {c_{0}}}&amp;{\hbox{(6)}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; \quad + \alpha_{3,k,l} s_{{\rm Tx},k}(t-\tau_{3,k,l}) &amp;{\hbox{(4)}}\cr\tau_{2,l} = &amp;\, {{\Vert {\bf z}_{\rm Tag}- {\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l} \Vert_{2}}\over {c_{0}}} &amp;{\hbox{(5)}}\cr\tau_{3,k,l} = &amp;\, {{\Vert {\bf z}_{{\rm Tx},k}- {\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l} \Vert_{2}}\over {c_{0}}}&amp;{\hbox{(6)}}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">{\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the position of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">l</script></tex-math></inline-formula>th receive antenna, with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l \in \left \{1,\ldots, M\right \}:l \ne k</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">l \in \left \{1,\ldots, M\right \}:l \ne k</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. This signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm RF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">s_{{\rm RF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is provided at the RF port of the quadrature demodulator, whose LO port is supported by a signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm LO},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">s_{{\rm LO},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> described by <disp-formula id="deqn7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm LO},l}(t) = A_{{\rm LO},l} \cos (\omega_{0} t + \varphi_{{\rm LO},l})\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-37">s_{{\rm LO},l}(t) = A_{{\rm LO},l} \cos (\omega_{0} t + \varphi_{{\rm LO},l})\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">s_{{\rm LO},l}(t) = A_{{\rm LO},l} \cos (\omega_{0} t + \varphi_{{\rm LO},l})\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{{\rm LO},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">A_{{\rm LO},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represents the amplitude, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm LO},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">\varphi_{{\rm LO},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the initial phase. This leads to an output signal at the IF port of the quadrature demodulator, which is filtered to obtain a passband around the modulation frequency of the RFID tag and sampled by an ADC. The resulting intermediate frequency signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">s_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be modeled by <disp-formula id="deqn8-10" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{s_{{\rm IF},k,l}(t) = &amp;\, A_{{\rm IF},k,l} {\rm e}^{j(\omega_{0} \tau_{k,l} + \phi_{k,l} - \varphi_{0,k,l})} s_{\rm ID}(t-\tau_{2,l}) &amp;{\hbox{(8)}}\cr\tau_{k,l} = &amp;\, \tau_{1,k} + \tau_{2,l} &amp;{\hbox{(9)}}\cr\varphi_{0,k,l} = &amp;\, \varphi_{{\rm Tx},k}-\varphi_{{\rm LO},l}&amp;{\hbox{(10)}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-41">\eqalignno{s_{{\rm IF},k,l}(t) = &amp;\, A_{{\rm IF},k,l} {\rm e}^{j(\omega_{0} \tau_{k,l} + \phi_{k,l} - \varphi_{0,k,l})} s_{\rm ID}(t-\tau_{2,l}) &amp;{\hbox{(8)}}\cr\tau_{k,l} = &amp;\, \tau_{1,k} + \tau_{2,l} &amp;{\hbox{(9)}}\cr\varphi_{0,k,l} = &amp;\, \varphi_{{\rm Tx},k}-\varphi_{{\rm LO},l}&amp;{\hbox{(10)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{s_{{\rm IF},k,l}(t) = &amp;\, A_{{\rm IF},k,l} {\rm e}^{j(\omega_{0} \tau_{k,l} + \phi_{k,l} - \varphi_{0,k,l})} s_{\rm ID}(t-\tau_{2,l}) &amp;{\hbox{(8)}}\cr\tau_{k,l} = &amp;\, \tau_{1,k} + \tau_{2,l} &amp;{\hbox{(9)}}\cr\varphi_{0,k,l} = &amp;\, \varphi_{{\rm Tx},k}-\varphi_{{\rm LO},l}&amp;{\hbox{(10)}}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">A_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represents the amplitude of the IF signal, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">\tau_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the time of flight, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">\phi_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is an additional phase shift depending on the orientation of the RFID tag. Due to the fact that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{0,k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">\varphi_{0,k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> specifies a constant phase offset describing various factors including cable length, this value can be compensated by calibration. The PoA <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is therefore a time-independent value described by <disp-formula id="deqn11" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l} = \underbrace {\omega_{0}\tau_{k,l}}_{\varphi_{k,l}} + \phi_{k,l} - \varphi_{0,k,l}\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-47">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l} = \underbrace {\omega_{0}\tau_{k,l}}_{\varphi_{k,l}} + \phi_{k,l} - \varphi_{0,k,l}\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l} = \underbrace {\omega_{0}\tau_{k,l}}_{\varphi_{k,l}} + \phi_{k,l} - \varphi_{0,k,l}\eqno{\hbox{(11)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">\varphi_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is depending on the time the signal takes to propagate from the position of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">k</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">k</script></tex-math></inline-formula>th transmit antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\bf z}_{{\rm Tx},k}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">{\bf z}_{{\rm Tx},k}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to the position of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">l</script></tex-math></inline-formula>th receive antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">{\bf z}_{{\rm Rx},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> via the position of the RFID tag <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\bf z}_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">{\bf z}_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and therefore contains the required information about the position of the RFID tag.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Influence of Tag Orientation</h3><p>As mentioned before, the orientation of the passive UHF RFID tag has an impact on the PoA. It is assumed that the tag used in the indoor positioning system can be modeled as a linear polarized dipole antenna with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec {P}_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">\vec {P}_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describing the direction of the polarization. If the coordinate system is located in the center of the right-handed circular polarized (RCP) antenna of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">l</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">l</script></tex-math></inline-formula>th receive channel according to the simplified model shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>, the direction of the electrical field <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> occurring at this receive antenna can be calculated by <disp-formula id="deqn12" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}} = \vec {P}_{\rm Tag} - {{\vec {P}_{\rm Tag} \vec {S}}\over{\vert \vec {S} \vert^{2}}} \vec {S} =\left[\matrix{\vert \vec {P}_{\vec {E}} \vert \cr\phi_{l} \cr \theta_{l}}\right]\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-57">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}} = \vec {P}_{\rm Tag} - {{\vec {P}_{\rm Tag} \vec {S}}\over{\vert \vec {S} \vert^{2}}} \vec {S} =\left[\matrix{\vert \vec {P}_{\vec {E}} \vert \cr\phi_{l} \cr \theta_{l}}\right]\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}} = \vec {P}_{\rm Tag} - {{\vec {P}_{\rm Tag} \vec {S}}\over{\vert \vec {S} \vert^{2}}} \vec {S} =\left[\matrix{\vert \vec {P}_{\vec {E}} \vert \cr\phi_{l} \cr \theta_{l}}\right]\eqno{\hbox{(12)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec {S}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">\vec {S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describes the Poynting vector, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec {n}_{{\rm Rx},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\vec {n}_{{\rm Rx},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the normal to the surface of the antenna. If spherical coordinates are used to describe <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">\vec {P}_{\vec {E}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, then <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">\phi_{l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is equal to the phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{{\rm RCP},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">\phi_{{\rm RCP},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> occurring at this receive antenna. Besides this phase shift, there also arises a phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> due to the transmit antenna, which is calculated in the exact same manner. The total phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that appears between transmit antenna, RFID tag, and receive antenna is calculated by <disp-formula id="deqn13" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k,l} = \phi_{{\rm RCP},k} + \phi_{{\rm RCP},l}.\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-65">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k,l} = \phi_{{\rm RCP},k} + \phi_{{\rm RCP},l}.\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\phi_{{\rm RCP},k,l} = \phi_{{\rm RCP},k} + \phi_{{\rm RCP},l}.\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>If left-handed circularly polarized (LCP) transceive antennas are used, the phase shift at each of the antennas exhibits a changed sign. For the estimation of the position of the RFID transponder, we assume that the orientation of the tag is known. Therefore, the usage of linear polarized (LP) transceive antennas can be advantageous. In this case, the phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{{\rm LP},l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\phi_{{\rm LP},l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for each antenna can be calculated by <disp-formula id="deqn14" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{{\rm LP},l} =\cases{0, &amp; for $\phi_{l} \in \left[- {{\pi}\over {2}},{{\pi}\over {2}} \right.\left[+2i\pi, i \in \BBN \right.$ \cr \pi, &amp; else.}\eqno{\hbox{(14)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-67">\phi_{{\rm LP},l} =\cases{0, &amp; for $\phi_{l} \in \left[- {{\pi}\over {2}},{{\pi}\over {2}} \right.\left[+2i\pi, i \in \BBN \right.$ \cr \pi, &amp; else.}\eqno{\hbox{(14)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\phi_{{\rm LP},l} =\cases{0, &amp; for $\phi_{l} \in \left[- {{\pi}\over {2}},{{\pi}\over {2}} \right.\left[+2i\pi, i \in \BBN \right.$ \cr \pi, &amp; else.}\eqno{\hbox{(14)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Signal Processing</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Phase Evaluation</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig><p>System demonstrator consisting of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M=8</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">M=8</script></tex-math></inline-formula> channels. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm I}k</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">{\rm I}k</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm Q}k</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">{\rm Q}k</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are the outputs of the demodulator for in-phase and quadrature, respectively. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm RF}k</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">{\rm RF}k</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the antenna port.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Influence of tag orientation using the example of a linear polarized RFID tag and a right-handed circular polarized receive antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
As previously mentioned, the PoA <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a time-independent value depending on the position and the orientation of the mobile RFID tag. An estimation of this PoA <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat {\varphi}}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">{\mathhat {\varphi}}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be obtained by <disp-formula id="deqn15-18" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{\rho_{k,l}[m] = &amp;\, \sum_{n=0}^{N-1} s_{{\rm IF},k,l}[n+m] s_{\rm ID}^{\ast}[n]&amp;{\hbox{(15)}}\cr{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l} = &amp;\, \arg \max_{m} \vert \rho_{k,l}[m] \vert&amp;{\hbox{(16)}}\cr{\mathhat {\eta}}_{k,l} = &amp;\, \vert \rho_{k,l}[{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}] \vert&amp;{\hbox{(17)}}\cr{\mathhat {\varphi}}_{{\rm IF},k,l} = &amp;\, \angle \rho_{k,l} [{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}]&amp;{\hbox{(18)}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-74">\eqalignno{\rho_{k,l}[m] = &amp;\, \sum_{n=0}^{N-1} s_{{\rm IF},k,l}[n+m] s_{\rm ID}^{\ast}[n]&amp;{\hbox{(15)}}\cr{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l} = &amp;\, \arg \max_{m} \vert \rho_{k,l}[m] \vert&amp;{\hbox{(16)}}\cr{\mathhat {\eta}}_{k,l} = &amp;\, \vert \rho_{k,l}[{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}] \vert&amp;{\hbox{(17)}}\cr{\mathhat {\varphi}}_{{\rm IF},k,l} = &amp;\, \angle \rho_{k,l} [{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}]&amp;{\hbox{(18)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{\rho_{k,l}[m] = &amp;\, \sum_{n=0}^{N-1} s_{{\rm IF},k,l}[n+m] s_{\rm ID}^{\ast}[n]&amp;{\hbox{(15)}}\cr{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l} = &amp;\, \arg \max_{m} \vert \rho_{k,l}[m] \vert&amp;{\hbox{(16)}}\cr{\mathhat {\eta}}_{k,l} = &amp;\, \vert \rho_{k,l}[{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}] \vert&amp;{\hbox{(17)}}\cr{\mathhat {\varphi}}_{{\rm IF},k,l} = &amp;\, \angle \rho_{k,l} [{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}]&amp;{\hbox{(18)}}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the number of samples. Due to the fact that the information communicated by the RFID tag contains its unique identification number <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{\rm ID}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">s_{\rm ID}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that is known in advance, the time-discrete cross correlation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">\rho_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the received IF signal <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">s_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{\rm ID}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">s_{\rm ID}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as function of time-lag <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be calculated. This leads to an estimation of the time lag <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">{\mathhat {m}}_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat {\eta}}_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">{\mathhat {\eta}}_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> describes the likelihood of the PoA estimation. Since the differences in the propagation time <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau_{2,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">\tau_{2,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the mobile tag to the receive antennas are negligible compared with the sampling period of the ADC, the estimated time-lag must be equal for all receive channels, and therefore a reduction in incorrect results can be achieved.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. Position Estimation</h3><p>The mobile RFID tag is localized on the basis of the PoA estimates <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">{\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">M</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-channel system demonstrator. It is assumed that the orientation of the RFID tag is known, therefore, the desired values for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">\varphi_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">\phi_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be calculated for each position covered by the localization system. If the constant phase offset <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{0,k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">\varphi_{0,k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is determined due to reference measurements, the desired values for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be calculated according to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn11" href="#deqn11" class="fulltext-link">(11)</a>. Because of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2\pi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">2\pi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> ambiguity in phase measurements, an infinite number of path lengths from the transmit antenna to each receive antenna via the tag exist that result in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">\varphi_{k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. For 2-D localization this results in curves of equal phase, each line describing an ellipse with the transmit antenna and the receive antenna located in the focal points. This is shown in simplified form for a system with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M=4</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">M=4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> channels in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Localization by means of PoA evaluation.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>To obtain a position estimation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat {\bf z}}_{\rm Tag}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">{\mathhat {\bf z}}_{\rm Tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the mobile RFID tag, a 2-D grid search algorithm is performed which discretizes the area covered by the localization system. For each of the resulting positions, the cosine similarity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">p</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">p</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between a matrix containing the desired values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> specified by <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn11" href="#deqn11" class="fulltext-link">(11)</a> and a matrix containing the PoA estimates <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">{\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is calculated according to <disp-formula id="deqn19" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">p({\bf z}_{\rm Tag}) = {\rm Re} \left ({{1}\over {M^{2}}} \sum_{k=1}^{M} \sum_{l=1}^{M} {\mathhat \eta}_{k,l} {\rm e}^{j(\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}({\bf z}_{\rm Tag}) - {\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l})} \right).\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-97">p({\bf z}_{\rm Tag}) = {\rm Re} \left ({{1}\over {M^{2}}} \sum_{k=1}^{M} \sum_{l=1}^{M} {\mathhat \eta}_{k,l} {\rm e}^{j(\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}({\bf z}_{\rm Tag}) - {\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l})} \right).\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">p({\bf z}_{\rm Tag}) = {\rm Re} \left ({{1}\over {M^{2}}} \sum_{k=1}^{M} \sum_{l=1}^{M} {\mathhat \eta}_{k,l} {\rm e}^{j(\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}({\bf z}_{\rm Tag}) - {\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l})} \right).\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span></span></disp-formula> This cosine similarity achieves its maximum for the best accordance of the phase values, thus allowing the position of the RFID tag to be estimated. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> shows the application of this algorithm to measurements carried out in an indoor environment using a system containing of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M=8</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">M=8</script></tex-math></inline-formula> channels.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>Cosine similarity <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">p</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">p</script></tex-math></inline-formula> between a matrix containing the desired values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">\varphi_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a matrix containing the PoA estimates <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">{\mathhat \varphi}_{{\rm IF},k,l}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of a mobile RFID tag based on measurements carried out in an indoor environment.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Measurement Results</h2></div><p>Measurements were carried out in an indoor environment to verify the accuracy of the localization system. The area covered by the position measurement system was defined to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\hbox{3 m} \times \hbox{3 m}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-102">\hbox{3 m} \times \hbox{3 m}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">M=8</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">M=8</script></tex-math></inline-formula> right-handed circular polarized transceive antennas were placed at the ceiling of the room pointing vertically downward. A passive UHF RFID transponder attached with known orientation to a 2-D traversing rail was moved to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N=645</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">N=645</script></tex-math></inline-formula> defined positions in the area covered by the localization system, with a distance between the tag plane and the antenna plane of 2.09 m. The carrier frequency of the signal generated by the RFID reader was set to four values from 865.7 to 867.5 MHz, and the radiated power to 2 W ERP. The median error of the position estimates is calculated as 0.036 m, and the root-mean-square deviation (RMSD) with <disp-formula id="deqn20" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm RMSD}({\mathhat {\bf z}}_{\rm Tag}) = \sqrt {{\sum_{n=1}^{N}\Vert {\bf z}_{{\rm Tag},n}- {\mathhat {\bf z}}_{{\rm Tag},n} \Vert_{2}^{2}}\over{N}}\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-105">{\rm RMSD}({\mathhat {\bf z}}_{\rm Tag}) = \sqrt {{\sum_{n=1}^{N}\Vert {\bf z}_{{\rm Tag},n}- {\mathhat {\bf z}}_{{\rm Tag},n} \Vert_{2}^{2}}\over{N}}\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm RMSD}({\mathhat {\bf z}}_{\rm Tag}) = \sqrt {{\sum_{n=1}^{N}\Vert {\bf z}_{{\rm Tag},n}- {\mathhat {\bf z}}_{{\rm Tag},n} \Vert_{2}^{2}}\over{N}}\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span></span></disp-formula> as 0.558 m. The measurements showed that 76.1% of the tag positions were estimated with an error less than 0.1 m. The probability distribution of the localization error is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>. Compared with the results showed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_6">[12]</a>, where the measurements were carried out in an anechoic chamber, the accuracy is slightly decreased. However, using the principle of combined transmit and receive antennas showed in this paper, the area covered by the measurement system can be increased by scaling up the system demonstrator and adding further antennas.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Distribution of the localization error based on 645 measurements with a moving passive UHF RFID tag in an indoor environment.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6677550/6657782/6657782-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>Localization by means of PoA evaluation in an indoor environment.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6657782/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
To reduce the number of inaccurate position estimations, a tracking algorithm was applied to the measurements. This algorithm determines the most likely sequence of tag positions using transition probabilities, which are supposed to be Gaussian distributed with an expectation of the distribution of 0 m and a standard deviation of 0.1 m. Using this algorithm, quick changes in the estimated tag position caused by inaccurate measurements can be avoided. This results in an improvement of the RMSD to 0.038 m, and 99.4% of the tag positions are estimated with an error of less than 0.1 m. The application of this algorithm as well as the measurement setup can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A multiple-channel position measurement system for passive UHF RFID tags based on PoA evaluation has been presented, where each channel can be configured as transmitter or receiver. The system uses an off-the-shelf RFID reader and existing passive EPC Gen 2 UHF RFID transponders. Measurements performed by means of a system demonstrator in an indoor environment showed excellent localization accuracy, especially when a tracking algorithm is applied.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
